рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

тАШрдХреЛ рдиреБ рд╡рд╛рдореН ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрдпреГрдЪрдВ рдирд╡рдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рднреМрдорд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреНрд░реЗрд░рд╛рд░реНрд╖рдореН ред рд╖реЛрдбрд╢реАрд╕рдкреНрддрджрд╢реНрдпрд╛рд╡рддрд┐рдЬрдЧрддреНрдпреМ рд╡рд┐рдВрд╢реНрдпреИрдХрдкрджрд╛ рд╡рд┐рд░рд╛рдЯреН рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдГ рд╕рдкреНрддрджрд╢ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдГ ред рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реЗ рджреЗрд╡рд╛ рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪрд╛рдиреБрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдВ-тАЩрдХреЛ рдиреБ рд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реИрд╢реНрд╡рджреЗрд╡рдВ рд╡реИ рддрддреН рд╖реЛрд│рд╢реНрдпрд╛рджреНрдпрддрд┐рдЬрдЧрддреНрдпрд╛рд╡рдиреНрддреНрдпреИрдХрдкрджрд╛’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧреЛ рд▓реИрдЩреНрдЧрд┐рдХрдГ редред

Jamison Brereton

41 (395)
All Gods
Atri Bhauma
20 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh, except atijagat─л 16тАУ17, ekapad─Б vir─Бj 20
This hymn is quite intricate on the verbal level, though in paraphrase and in translation it may seem to lack interest. Every verse (but 17) names at least one divinityтАФmany verses have severalтАФchosen from among both the most promi nent gods of the Vedic pantheon (e.g., Mitra and Varuс╣Зa in vs. 1) and distinctly marginal figures like ─Аptya (vs. 9). There does not seem to be any one dominant god or set of gods: though the Maruts are mentioned more than any other gods (vss. 2, 5, 11, 13, 16), there is little particularly Marutian vocabulary or imagery. (It might be remembered, however, that the longest series of Marut hymns in the R╠еgveda, the ┼Ъy─Бv─Б┼Ыva hymns of remarkable poetic quality, immediately follow the All God hymns in this maс╣Зс╕Нala [V.52тАУ61]). The content of the hymn as a whole seldom deviates from invitations to the sacrifice with promises of offerings, and prayers for divine gifts in return. Verses 16тАУ17 are in a different meter and seem to be bringing the hymn to a close, especially 17, in which, as often, the poet makes a meta-reference to the hymn just concluded. If this is so, verses 18тАУ20 are an afterthought.
The seemingly unordered series of gods who receive the honor of a verse (or part thereof) may exemplify a covert theme of choice or alternatives, underlined by the

use of the simple conjunction тАЬorтАЭ (v─Б) as the verbal тАЬheroтАЭ of the beginning of the hymn (vss. 1тАУ3, returning at the end, vss. 15, 19).
Unfortunately other pieces of verbal play are essentially untranslatable, like the unusual sequence of two monosyllables at the end of the first half-verse of verse 1:… v─Б d├й (тАЬor…to be givenтАЭ), which, scrambled, produces the target of the hymn: dev─Б(с╕е) тАЬgods.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

All Gods As noted in the published introduction, the hymn consists of verses dedicated to a sequence of gods, both major and minor, seemingly unordered. The full list consists of 1 Mitra and Varuс╣Зa / 2 Mitra, Varuс╣Зa, ─Аyu, Indra, Maruts, Rudra / 3 A┼Ыvins, Rudra / 4 Trita, Wind, Agni, P┼лс╣гan, Bhaga / 5 Maruts / 6 V─Бyu / 7 Night and Dawn / 8 Men (Maruts?), Lord of the Dwelling Place, Tvaс╣гс╣нar, trees, plants, Holy Place / 9 Mountains, ─Аptya / 10 Trita, Ap─Бm Nap─Бt, Agni / 11 Maruts, Bhaga, waters, plants, woods, mountains / 12 Agni, Waters / 13 Maruts / 14 Indra (maybe) / 15 Shielding Goddess, Ras─Б / 16 Maruts, Ahi Budhnya / 17 gods / 18 gods, goddess / 19-20 Iс╕Н─Б, Urva┼Ы─л. The Maruts regularly recur in this sequence, and though, as noted in the published

introduction, there is little Marut imagery (though perhaps more vocab. than I recognized at the time), if there is focus in this hymn, it is probably the Maruts, who dominate much of the rest of the maс╣Зс╕Нala after the All God hymns.

рд╣реЗ рдорд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд░реБрдгреМ рджреЗрд╡реМ рд╡рд╛рдВ рдпреБрд╡рд╛ рдХреЛ рдиреБ рдХрдГ рдЦрд▓реБ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирдГ рдЛрддрд╛рдпрдиреН рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫрдиреН рд╢рдХреНрдиреБрдпрд╛рджрд┐рддрд┐ рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ ред рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреН рдХреГрдкрдпреИрд╡ рджрд┐рд╡рдГ рд╕рджрд╕рд┐ рджреНрдпреБрд▓реЛрдХрд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐рдирд┐ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЗ рдорд╣рдГ рдорд╣рддрдГ рдкрд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рд╡рд╕реНрдп рд╕рджрд╕рд┐ ред рдЛрддрд╕реНрдп рдЙрддреНрдкрд╛рджрдХрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╕реНрдп рд╕рджрд╕рд┐ ред рддрджреНрдзреЗрддреБрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреНрддрд╛рдЪреНрдЫрдмреНрджреНрдпрдореН ред рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реБ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЗрд╖реБ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рддреНрд░рд╛рд╕реАрдерд╛рдВ рд░рдХреНрд╖рддрдореНред рд╡рд╛рд╢рдмреНрджрд╢реНрдЪрд╛рд░реНрдереЗ ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдпрддреЗ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫрддреЗ рджреЗ рд╡рд╛ рд╣рд╡рд┐рд░реНрджрд╛рддреНрд░реЗ рдЪ рдорд╣реНрдпрдВ рдкрд╢реБрд╖реЛ рди рд╡рд╛рдЬрд╛рдиреН рдкрд╢реБрд╖реБ рд╕реАрджрддреЛ рд╡рд╛рдЬрд╛рдирдиреНрдирд╛рдирд┐ рдХреНрд╖реАрд░рджрдзреНрдпрд╛рджреАрдиреАрд╡ ред рддрд╛рдирд┐ рдпрдерд╛ рдкреНрд░рдпрдЪреНрдЫрдердГ рддрджреНрд╡рджрд╡рддрдорд┐рддрд┐ ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рдирд╢рдмреНрджрд╢реНрдЪрд╛рд░реНрдереЗ ред рдкрд╢реБрд╖рдГ рдкрд╢реВрдиреНрд╡рд╛рдЬрд╛рдВрд╢реНрдЪ рджрддреНрддрдорд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWho, Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, desiring to sacrifice to you, (is able to do so)? do you, whether (abiding) in the region of heaven, or of the vast earth, or of the firmament, protect us, and give to the donor (of the oblation), and to the sacrificer, cattle and food.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Which one now, performing the truth for you two, Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, is to be given (a good thing) from great heaven or one stemming from
the earth
or (one) at the seat of truth [=ritual ground]тАФyou two should protect usтАФor which of you two (is ready) to give prizes to the sacrificer like the prizes for one who wins cattle?

Jamison Brereton Notes

The conjunction v─Б тАШorтАЩ dominates this vs.: there are 4 overt occurrences (twice in b, once each in c and d), as well as covert encodings, beginning with v─Б(m mitr)─Бv(aruс╣З)─Бv (the latter two inverted) in p─Бda a and ending with the last word of the vs., v─Б╠Б(j─Бn). The end of the 2nd p─Бda, v─Б d├й, with two monosyllables that, inverted, produce d├йv─Б(с╕е) (though with wrong accent for *dev─Б╠Бс╕е), draws further attention to v─Б.

As noted in the introduction, the prominence of v─Б may establish a theme of choice or alternatives appropriate to the mass of gods mentioned in the rest of the hymn, and v─Б also echoes the last syllable of the phrase v├н┼Ыve dev─Б╠Бс╕е тАЬAll Gods,тАЭ to whom the hymn is dedicated.

Given the plethora of v─Б-s and the absence of any finite verb, save for intrusive tr─Б╠Бs─лth─Бm in c, it is not surprising that interpretations of the structure and syntax of the vs. are all over the map. In addition to the standard tr. (Geldner, Renou [EVP IV, V], Witzel Got┼Н), see also Oldenberg, L├╝ders (Varuс╣Зa 585-86), Schindler (Root nouns, 24-25), Klein (II.203-4), Scarlatta (581), Keydana (Inf. 155 n. 142). I will not rehearse them all here.

Like many of these interpr., I take the three v─Б-s of bc as defining a tripartite structure of roughly parallel entities. I then assume that the v─Б of d is situated on a higher level of structure and is contrasting abc with a new clause inaugurated in d.

The two clauses (abc and d) are separated by the independent interjection tr─Бs─лth─Бс╣Г naс╕е closing c. As Geldner points out (n. 1c), tr─Бs─лth─Бс╣Г naс╕е has a similar role elsewhere (IV.55.1, VII.71.2); IV.55.1 is especially similar, since it is in the first vs. of an All God hymn that begins k├│ vaс╕е (like k├│ n├║ v─Бm here), with Mitra and Varuс╣Зa as the subjects of tr─Б╠Бs─лth─Бm.

My interpr. of the larger structure rests on taking d├й at the end of b as an infin.

(with many, but not all) and assuming that the poet has exploited the voice neutrality of infinitives to give it passive value in abc (тАЬ[is] to be givenтАЭ) and active value in d (тАЬ[is] to giveтАЭ). This further assumes that k├бс╕е refers to the (mortal) recipient in abc and, resupplied in d, to one of the gods. With these assumptions in place, the case relations in the two syntactically distinct parts of the vs. fall into place: the nom. k├бс╕е тАж с╣Ыt─Бy├бn тАЬwho, performing the truth тАжтАЭ of p─Бda a is the mortal worshiper and recipient of the godsтАЩ largess; his counterpart in d is the dat. yaj├▒─Бyat├й. The v─Бm of p─Бda a is to be interpr. two different ways: in the first part it expresses the divine beneficiaries of the mortalтАЩs service; resupplied in d, it should be construed with likewise resupplied k├бс╕е (or better katar├бс╕е) тАЬwhich of you two?тАЭ The tripartite v─Б structure of bc details the three sources of gifts that may be given to the worshiper: heaven, earth, and the ritual ground. They are subtly unparallel: тАШheavenтАЩ is a straight noun, either in abl. (as in the published translation) or gen.; earth is represented by a deriv. adj. тАШearthlyтАЩ in the gen. (p─Б╠Бrthivasya). It is a partitive gen., and if div├бс╕е тАж m├бhaс╕е is gen., it too is partitive. If itтАЩs an abl., it expresses the source.

The third term, тАЬat the seat of truthтАЭ (с╣Ыt├бsya тАж s├бdasi), expresses the place where the gift is to be given. Scarlatta supplies тАШat the seatтАЩ for all three terms. This is not impossible, but the poet seems to be aiming for slightly skewed and off-balance phraseology, and three different types of expressions for three parallel terms would suit his purposes admirably.

In the new structure of d, with active value of the infinitive d├й, v─Б╠Бj─Бn is its object. The last grammatically unparallel functional parallel is yaj├▒─Бyat├й тАж pa┼Ыuс╣г├│ n├б. Assuming that it is a gen. sg. (Oldenberg and Renou take it as acc. pl.), pa┼Ыuс╣г├бс╕е тАШof one who wins cattleтАЩ is in some sense parallel to yaj├▒─Бyat├й тАШfor the one who sacrificesтАЩ, in that the v─Б╠Бj─Бn (тАШprizesтАЩ) come to both. But pa┼Ыuс╣г├бс╕е is a gen. dependent on v─Б╠Бj─Бn, while yaj├▒─Бyat├й is the indirect object with the infin. d├й.

Griffith

WHO, Mitra-Varuna, is your pious servant to give you gifts from earth or mighty heaven?
Preserve us in the seat of holy Order, and give the offerer power that winneth cattle.

Geldner

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay those divinities, Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, Aryaman, ─Аyu, Indra, с╣Ъbhukс╣гin, the Maruts who accept pious praise, be plural ased by our adorations, partaking of the gratification afforded to Rudra, the showerer (of benefits).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Divinities who accept pious praise: divinities are of two orders, those who share praises, stotrabh─Бjaс╕е, and those who share oblations havirbh─Бjaс╕е, the first is here alluded to; Rudra the showerer: the last clause may allude to the Maruts as the sons of Rudra

Jamison Brereton

TheyтАФMitra, Varuс╣Зa, Aryaman, ─Аyu, Indra lord of the R╠еbhus, and the MarutsтАФshall take pleasure in us,
or (in those) who with reverences provide a well-plaited (hymn), a praise for Rudra who gives rewardsтАФ(they, the gods) in joint enjoyment.

Jamison Brereton Notes

After the catтАЩs cradle of vs. 1, this vs. comes as a welcome relief – or at least in its first half, which consists of a list of gods in the nom. and a verb they can all serve as subject to. With 6 gods (and an epithet – or 7 gods if с╣Ыbhukс╣г─Б╠Бis taken separately) to fit into 22 syllables, the poet canтАЩt get into too much trouble.

The 2nd hemistich is slightly more complex. It consists of an elliptical v─Б rel.

cl.: тАЬor (in those) who тАж,тАЭ with the gapped тАШthoseтАЩ parallel to enclitic naс╕е in p─Бda a.

The final word saj├│с╣г─Бс╕е I take as referring to the gods; the stem(s) saj├│с╣гa(s)- is generally used of gods (see saj├│с╣г─Бс╕е in 4b), and note that their verb juс╣гanta ends the first hemistich. But, with the standard tr., it may refer to the mortals providing the godsтАЩ praise.

Griffith

May Mitra, Varuna, Aryaman, and Ayu, Indra Rbhuksan, and the Maruts, love us,
And they who of one mind with bounteous Rudra accept the hymn and laud with adorations.

Geldner

Mitra, Varuna, Aryaman, Ayu, Indra, Ribhuksan, die Marut m├╢gen Wohlgefallen an uns haben oder an denen, die unter Verbeugungen ein Preislied darbringen, einen Lobgesang auf den belohnenden Rudra im Einvernehmen mit den G├╢ttern.

Grassmann

Hold sei’n uns Mitra, Arjaman, Varuna, Ribhukschan, Aju, Indra und die Maruts, Und denen hold, die im Vereine Loblied und Preis dem gn├дd’gen Rudra weihn in Demuth.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрдирдпрд╛рд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдиреМ рд░реБрджреНрд░рд╢реНрдЪреЛрдЪреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ ред рд╣реЗ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдирд╛ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдиреМ рдпреЗрд╖реНрдард╛ рдХрд╛рдорд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдпрдиреНрддреГрддрдореМ рд╡рд╛рдВ рдпреБрд╡рд╛рдВ рд╡рд╛рддрд╕реНрдп рдкрддреНрдордиреН ред рдзрд░реНрдорд╕рд╛рдореНрдпрд╛рджреНрдзрд░реНрдорд┐рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдгрдореН ред рд╡рд╛рдпреБрд╕рдорд╛рдирдЧрддреЗрд░рд╢реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рдЧрдордиреЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддреМ рд░рдереНрдпрд╕реНрдп рд░рдерд╕реНрдп рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯреМ рдЪ рдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрддреЗ рд╕рддрд┐ рд╣реБрд╡рдзреНрдпреИ рд╣реБрд╡реЗ рдЖрд╣реНрд╡рдпрд╛рдорд┐ рдЖрд╣реНрд╡рд╛рддреБрдВ рдкреНрд░рднрд╡рд╛рдорд┐ ред рдЕрдерд╡рд╛ рд╡рд╛рдпреБрд╡рджреНрдпреБрд╡рдпреЛрдГ рд╢реАрдШреНрд░рдЧрдордирд╕рд╛рдзрдирд░рдерд╕реНрдп рдкреЛрд╖реЗ рдЪ рдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрддреЗ рд╕рддрд┐ ред рдЙрдд рд╡рд╛ рдХрд┐рдВрдЪреЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГред рджрд┐рд╡рдГ рджреНрдпреЛрддрдорд╛рдирд╛рдп рее рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдереНрдпрд░реНрдереЗ рд╖рд╖реНрдареА рее рдЕрд╕реБрд░рд╛рдп рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдкрд╣рд░реНрддреНрд░реЗ рд░реБрджреНрд░рд╛рдп ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рджреНрдпреБрд▓реЛрдХрд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐рдиреЗрд╜рд╕реБрд░рд╛рдп рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрджрд╛рддреНрд░реЗ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╛рдп рд╡рд╛рдпрд╡реЗ рд╡рд╛ рдпрдЬреНрдпрд╡реЗ рдпрд╛рдЧрд╕рд╛рдзрдХрд╛рдп рдордиреНрдо рдордирдиреАрдп рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░рдВ рдкреНрд░ рднрд░рдзреНрд╡рдВ рд╕рдВрдкрд╛рджрдпрдд рд╣реЗ рдЛрддреНрд╡рд┐рдЬрдГ ред рдЕрдиреНрдзрд╛рдВрд╕реАрд╡ рдЕрдиреНрдирд╛рдирд┐ рд╣рд╡рд┐рд░реНрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рдирд┐ рд╣рд╡реАрдВрд╖рд┐ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░рдВ рдЪреЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI invoke you, A┼Ыvins, the restrainers (of desire), for the acceleration ofyour chariot with the swiftness of the wind; (priests) offer praise and oblations to the celestial destroyer of life, to the accmplisher of the sacrifice.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Celestial destroyer of life: divo asur─Бya = dyotam─Бn─Бya pr─Бс╣З─Бpahartre, that is, to Rudra;

Yajyave = y─Бgas─Бdhak─Бya;

Asura = pr─Бс╣Зad─Бt─Б, the giver, of life, when it will imply S┼лrya or V─Бyu

Jamison Brereton

You two A┼Ыvins, driving quickest on the flight of the wind, in the flourishing of your chariotry, are to be summoned hither.
Or (you priests), present a thought to the lord of heaven [=Rudra], like (soma) stalks to the worshipful.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I take the passively used inf. huv├бdhyai with a gapped agent тАЬby the priestsтАЭ vel sim., to match the implicit 2nd pl. subj. of pr├б тАж bharadhvam in the 2nd hemistich.

The use of a passive inf. in the 1st half, contrasting with an active usage (though not an inf. here) in the 2nd half, recalls the structure of vs. 1. In our vs. there is a switch of 2nd ps. reference from the (two) gods in ab to the (pl.) mortal officiants in cd.

The use of the derived adj. r├бthya- тАШbelonging to the chariotтАЩ rather than its base noun r├бtha- recalls p─Б╠Бrthivasya in 1c substituting for a form of the noun pс╣Ыthiv─л╠Б-.

Geldner (flg. S─Бyaс╣Зa.) identifies the тАЬlord of heavenтАЭ (div├│ ├бsura-) as Rudra, on the basis of parallels (see his n. 3c).

Griffith

You will I call to feed the car-horse, Asvins, with the wind’s flight swiftest of those who travel:
Or also to the Asura of heaven, Worshipful, bring a hymn as ’twere libation.

Geldner

Euch, Asvin, will ich herrufen, die ihr am ehesten kommt im Fluge des Windes, im Vollbesitz des Wagengeschirrs. Oder setzet dem Asura, dem Gebieter des Himmels, dem Opferverlangenden eine Dichtung ebenso wie die Somatr├дnke vor!

Grassmann

Euch Ritter ruf’ ich, die ihr fahrt aufs beste, im Flug des Windes, in des Rosses Eile; Und auch dem Geist des Himmels bringt Gebete wie Somatr├дnke dar dem hochverehrten.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the divine accepter of sacrifice, of whom the Kaс╣Зvas are the priests, Tс╣Ыta, V─Бyu and Agni, concurring in satisfaction with (the ruler of) heaven, or (S┼лrya and) P┼лс╣гan and Bhaga, and they who are the protectors of the universe, (come quickly) to the sacrifice, as the fleet course rush to battle.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Trita: may be an epithet of V─Бyu; the threefold, pervading the three regions of heaen, mid-air and earth

Jamison Brereton

The heavenly victor with Kaс╣Зva as Hotar, (i.e.,) Trita from heaven, and the Wind, and Agni in joint enjoyment,
P┼лс╣гan, and all-nourishing Bhaga have come to the (ritual) presentation like those with swiftest horses to a contest.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The parade of ill-assorted divinities and semi-divinities continues. The sequence is made more muddled by the fact that Trita is always a shadowy figure, who is probably (but not certainly) the same as ─Аptya in vs. 9 (─Аptya being TritaтАЩs usual patronymic) and Trita in 10 and who is probably (but not certainly) the referent of p─Бda a here: тАЬthe heavenly victor with Kaс╣Зva as Hotar.тАЭ If he is the referent of p─Бda a, it is slightly odd that he is both qualified as тАШheavenlyтАЩ (divy├бс╕е) and said to be тАШfrom heavenтАЩ (div├бс╕е, p─Бda b). It might be best, with Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) to take div├бс╕е as the place-from-which of all the figures mentioned; however, Wind and Agni are normally associated with the midspace and the earth respectively, and P┼лс╣гan and Bhaga are not particularly heavenly deities. ItтАЩs worth noting that divy├б- continues the poetтАЩs habit of using deriv. -ya-adjectives in place of (or perhaps here beside) their nominals, and so the doubling divy├б- / div├бс╕е might not be so odd after all.

I do not know exactly what to do with pr├б initial in the vs., but it is noteworthy that it fits into a sequence of pr├б-initial expressions, where the preverb is in tmesis, beginning with 3d pr├б тАж bharadhvam and continuing with 5a pr├б тАж bharadhvam again and 6a pr├б тАж kс╣Ыс╣Зudhvam (followed by initial pr├б in 6b and 7b).

In our vs. there is no finite verb to construe it with in tmesis, but note the loc. prabhс╣Ыth├й in c. My assumption is that vs.-initial pr├б simply reinforces prabhс╣Ыth├й in a vs. sandwiched between two full pr├б тАж bharadhvam expressions. It could also be construed with jagmuс╕е in d, though one might expect a more prominent, metricalboundary-adjoining jagmuс╕е in that case.

The loc. prabhс╣Ыth├й and the acc. ─Бj├нm both serve as goal with jagmuс╕е – another ex. of the poetтАЩs penchant for slightly off-balance parallels.

Griffith

The heavenly Victor, he whose priest is Kanva, Trta with Dyaus accordant, Vata, Agni,
All-feeding Pusan, Bhaga sought the oblation, as they whose steeds are fleetest seek the contest.

Geldner

Vom Himmel sind eintr├дchtig der himmlische Antreiber Trita, dessen Opferpriester Kanva war, und Vata, Agni, Pusan, Bhaga, der Allspeisende zu der Darbringung ausgezogen wie die Besitzer der schnellsten Rosse zum Wettlauf.

Grassmann

Des Himmels Sieger, welchem Kanva opfert, des Himmels Trita, Feuer, Wind vereinigt; Beim Opfer allern├дhrend Bhaga, Puschan, sie kamen wie zum Kampf mit schnellsten Rossen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMaruts, do you bring wealth comprising horses; to acquire and preserve riches the wise man offers you praise; may the ministrant priest, (Atri), of the son of U┼Ыij (Kakс╣г─лvat), be made happy by those swift-going (horses) which are the swift-going (horses), Maruts, of you who are rapid in motion.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Present your wealth of yoked horses; for help in the quest for wealth a visionary thought should be produced.
The Hotar [=Agni] is well disposed because of the ways of (the company of) fire-priests, which are (also?) the ways of you powerful ones, o
Maruts.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first hemistich consists of a syntactically тАЬactiveтАЭ 2nd pl. verb (тАШpresent!тАЩ pr├б тАж bharadhvam, though it is morphologically middle) paired with a passive (тАШshould be producedтАЩ dadh─лta) without overt agent, structurally similar to vs. 3 with a passive infinitive (huv├бdhyai) without agent and the same тАЬactiveтАЭ 2nd pl. pr├б тАж bharadhvam. This structure is further reminiscent of vs. 1 with passive and act. uses of the same infinitive d├й.

In this vs. it is not altogether clear who the 2nd pl. subject of pr├б bharadhvam is. Geldner thinks this is about the dakс╣гiс╣З─Б and suggests as subj. either the Opferveranstalter or the Maruts. I donтАЩt see the dakс╣гiс╣З─Б connection, and given the reciprocal relationship between gods and men depicted already in the hymn (vss. 1 and 3), in the next vs. (6) with dhiy├й dhuс╕е playing off dadh─лta dh─л╠Бс╕е in our 5b, and elsewhere, I think it likely that the 2nd pl. addressees here are the (All) Gods in general, who are asked to provide tangible wealth in exchange for the praise embodied in the dh─л╠Б- тАШvisionary thoughtтАЩ produced by the poets. The use of the exact same verb pr├б bharadhvam in 3 and 5, with opposite but complementary subjects (priest-poets / gods), is a neat reversal.

The standard tr. take au┼Ыij├бsya as a PN and construe it with h├│t─Б. This is not impossible, but since, as weтАЩve seen, the poet is fond of using -ya-deriv. adjectives for nouns, I think it more likely that it stands for u┼Ыij- тАШ(type of) priestтАЩ in the pl.

Assuming as usual, that the Hotar is Agni, who mediates between men and gods, it is reasonable that he would be pleased both by the activities of this priestly group and by those of the gods, represented by the Maruts. For the association of Hotar and au┼Ыij├б- see also IV.21.6-7, though that passage is exceptionally opaque.

The vs. contains several instances of phonological and morphological play. In b the p─Бda-final phrase dadh─лta dh─л╠Бс╕е shows tight phonological similarity though the two words belong to different roots. The same play is found in the next vs. (6d), likewise p─Бda-final, in dhiy├й dhuс╕е – same noun dh─л╠Б-, verb to the same root тИЪdh─Б – though the phonological relationship is not as tight. In 5b dadh─лta dh─л╠Бс╕е yields a very bad Triс╣гс╣нubh cadence, whereas 6d dhiy├й dhuс╕е provides a completely orthodox cadence. This may be an example of metrical poetic repair, where the metrical violation of the first calls attention to the phrase, which is satisfactorily resolved in the next vs. In the second hemistich we find # (su┼Ы)├йva ├йva(ir) … # (y)├й va ├йv─Б, evoking (d)eva- again. P─Бda d lacks a syllable. It is tempting to emend the opening to y├й *v─Б va ├йv─Б, given the prominence of v─Б in the hymn – as Oldenberg also suggests. But this emended sequence makes less sense and also disturbs its phonological echo of p─Бda c.

It should also be noted that y├й va ├йv─Б is also found in 13a in a different metrical position and cf. also scrambled evay─Б╠Бin 16b. If *v─Б were to be inserted, the tr. could be changed to тАЬis well disposed because of the ways of the тАж Priests or (those) which are the ways of you powerful ones, o Maruts.тАЭ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPrevail, (priests), by your prayers, on V─Бyu, the divine, the fulfiller of desires, the adorable, to harness his chariot; may the light-moving accepters of sacrifice, the lovely and excellent wives (of the gods), come hither to our rite.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Set V─Бyu, who hitches up the chariot, in front; in front the god, the inspired admirer, with your chantsтАФ
(you,) aiming (straight), serving the truth, (set in front) the creators of plenty. Let them, (like?) good wives, create (plenty) here (in exchange) for our visionary thought.

Jamison Brereton Notes

There are again a number of ways to construe this vs., and I will concentrate on my own. Given the alternation I see in this hymn between the actions of gods and men, I think (with most) that the 2nd pl. subj. of pr├б тАж kс╣Ыс╣Зudhvam is back to the mortal ritual officiants (as in 3cd), rather than the gods (as in 5a). I also take pr├б kс╣Ыс╣Зudhvam to be the verb of all of abc, reinforced by pr├б opening b. This further means that the nominatives of c (iс╣гudhy├бva с╣Ыtas─Б╠Бpaс╕е) refer to the mortals and the p├║raс╣Гdh─лс╕е is acc. pl., not nom. as many take it. Crucial to this interpr. is the parallel cited by Oldenberg, X.64.7 pr├б vo v─Б╠Бyuс╣Г rathay├║jaс╣Г p├║raс╣Гdhiс╣Г, st├│maiс╕е krс╣З╠е udhvam sakhy─Б╠Бya p┼лс╣г├бс╣Зam. тАЬSet in front with your praises V─Бyu, who hitches up the chariot, Plenitude, (and) P┼лс╣гan for partnership,тАЭ with clear acc. p├║raс╣Гdhim a parallel obj.

with v─Б╠Бyuс╣Г rathay├║jam (as here) to pr├б тАж kс╣Ыс╣Зudhvam.

I then take d as displaying the usual reciprocity found elsewhere in the hymn, but with a grammatical twist. The last set of divine beings honored by mortals, the acc. object p├║raс╣Гdhi- of c, are, in my opinion, the unexpressed subjects of d and participate in a grammatical play. The noun p├║raс╣Гdhi- is fem., though it is at most the animatization of an abstract тАШplenitude, abundanceтАЩ. Furthermore, it looks synchronically like a cmpd. with a form of тИЪdh─Б, even though that is not the current standard etym. (cf. EWA s.v.). I therefore think that the pl. obj. p├║raс╣Гdh─лс╕е of p─Бda c, reconfigured as subjects of d, are depicted as explicitly female – as тАШgood wivesтАЩ (v├бsv─лс╕е тАж p├бtn─лс╕е) – and serve as subject to a form of тИЪdh─Б (dhuс╕е) folketymologically extracted from p├║raс╣Гdhi-. The unexpressed obj. is then (missegmented) *p├║ram *тАШplentyтАЩ. As was discussed ad vs. 5, dhuс╕е also participates in a figure with dhiy├й that reverses dadh─лta dh─л╠Бс╕е in 5d.

I do not entirely understand the position of ─Б╠Б, which appears to be a preverb with dhuс╕е (so Grassmann), but appears to have been moved in tmesis to a position adjacent neither to a metrical boundary nor to a syntactic one (though this would be easier to argue). It may have been flipped (from a putative *dhiy├й ─Б╠Бdhuс╕е) to allow the figure just discussed (dhiy├й dhuс╕е picking up 5b dadh─лta dh─л╠Бс╕е).

On iс╣гudhy├║-, see comm. ad I.128.6 and my forthcoming article тАЬVedic iс╣гudhy├б- and Oldenberg Avestan i┼бud-, i┼б┼лidiia-: The Aim of Praise.тАЭ

Griffith

Bring hither him who yokes the car, your Vayu, who praises with his songs, the God and Singer;
And, praying and devout, noble and prudent, may the Gods’ Spouses in their thoughts retain us.

Geldner

Machet den seinen Wagen schirrenden Vayu geneigt, machet den redekundigen Gott, den Anerkennenden, mit Preisliedern geneigt - auf Belohnungen Anspruch erhebend als Pfleger der Wahrheit. M├╢gen die guten Gattinnen der G├╢tter unserem Gedicht sie dabei gew├дhren.

Grassmann

Den Vaju stellt euch an als Wagenschirrer, den Gott als S├дnger, der mit Liedern preise, Die frommen, guten, reichen G├╢tterfrauen sie m├╢gen strebend uns zur Andacht f├╢rdern.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMighty Day and Night, to you, along with the adorable (deities) of heaven, I present (the oblation) with prayers delighting and explicit; knowing, like two sages, all (that is required), do you bring (it) to the worshipper for his sacrifice.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

I hasten to the two young maidens of heaven with your praiseworthy fortifying (hymns), with conspicuous chants.
Night and Dawn, like ones who know all, through the days convey the sacrifice here for the mortal.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The hymn contains three exx. of ├йс╣гe (5b, 7a, 8d). Though Lubotsky classifies them all as locc. to the thematic stem ├йс╣гa-, I follow the standard tr. in taking the one in this vs. as a 1st sg. pres., while the other two are locc. in the phrase r─Бy├б ├йс╣гe тАЬin the quest for wealth.тАЭ The parallel for 7a cited by Geldner, I.186.4 ├║pa va ├йс╣гe тАж uс╣г─Б╠Бs─Бn├бkt─Б, seems to clinch this interpr., and the next vs. (8), beginning abh├н vo arce, also PREV vaс╕е 1st - sg. VERB, reinforces it. In d I read ─Б╠Бh─Б not ─Б╠Бh─Б (a change only in the Pp. not the Saс╣Гhit─Б text), and analyze this sequence as ─Б╠Б+ ├бh─Б, the neut. pl. of тАШdayтАЩ. This is one of only two supposed exx. of the particle ha with long vowel; the other one (IV.31.5) also follows ─Б╠Бand is susceptible to the same analysis. See disc. there.

Griffith

I speed to you with powers that should be honoured, with songs distinguishing Heaven’s mighty Daughters,
Morning and Night, the Two, as ’twere all-knowing: these bring the sacrifice unto the mortal.

Geldner

Ich wende mich f├╝r euch mit l├╢blichen anspornenden Worten an die beiden j├╝ngsten T├╢chter des Himmels mit ausgezeichneten Preisliedern: Die Morgenr├╢te und die Nacht, die gleichsam alles wissen, bringen dem Sterblichen das Opfer mit.

Grassmann

Ich geh euch an mit preisenswerthen Liedern; mit lichten Strahlen fahren jedes Opfer Des Himmels T├╢chter, Nacht und Morgenr├╢the, dem Sterblichen, sich wohl darauf verstehend.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI glorify you, leaders (of rites), cherishers (of many), gratifying (with oblation, you) Tvaс╣гс╣н─Б the lord of foundations, and the goddess of speech, bestower of opulence, and share in the satisfaction (of the other divinities); also the lords of the forest, and the herbs, that I may obtain riches.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

I chant for you to the men granting prosperity, to the Lord of the Dwelling-Place, to Tvaс╣гс╣нar, as I give;
with reverences (I chant) to the trees, the plants, along with the rich Holy Place, in the quest for wealth.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner takes nс╣Ы╠Б╠Дn as gen. pl. rather than acc., but this is unnec. The stem nс╣Ы╠Б- is regularly used of gods, esp. the Maruts, so there is no reason that they cannot be addressees here (so Renou, Witzel Got┼Н).

The standard tr. take dh├бny─Б saj├│с╣г─Б dhiс╣г├бс╣З─Б as nom. sg. and parenthetic; e.g., Geldner тАЬтАФeinverstanden ist die reichmachende Dhiс╣гaс╣З─БтАФтАЭ But the instr. sg. in -─Б to fem.

-─Б-stems is still quite common in the RV, and that is how I construe the phrase here.

Griffith

You I extol, the nourishers of heroes bringing you gifts, Vastospati and Tvastar-
Rich Dhisana accords through our obeisance - andTrees and Plants, for the swift gain of riches.

Geldner

Ich besinge opferspendend f├╝r euch die Gedeihenbringer der Menschen, den Vastospati und Tvastri - einverstanden ist die reichmachende Dhisana - unter Verbeugungen, die B├дume, die Pflanzen im Streben nach Reichtum.

Grassmann

Ich preise euch, die segensreichen M├дnner, den Hauses Hort und Tvaschtar, Gaben opfernd, Mit Demuth beide reichen Weltenschalen, die B├дum’ und Kr├дuter geh ich an um Reichthum.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the Parvatas be (bountiful) to us in liberal donations; may they be favourable (to us) who are the establishers (of the world) like heroes; may the adored and adorable (deity), who is accessible (to all), who is friendly to man, ever grant us increase, being propitiated by our praise.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The Parvatas: the clouds; in liberal donations: tuje nastane: tane = vistс╣Ыte, expanded;

Tuje = d─Бne, gift; or, tuje = son;

Tane = grandson; accessible to all: ─Бptyo yajataс╕е: ─Бptyo = ─Бptavyaс╕е sarvaiс╕е, to be obtained by all;

Yajataс╕е = yajan─лya, to be worshipped, that is, ─Аditya; propitiated by our praise: naс╕е ┼Ыaс╣Гsam abhiс╣гс╣нau = our praise in seeking or approaching

Jamison Brereton

Let the mountains behave like family, to thrust out progeny for usтАФ they who are like good heroes.
─Аptya, admired, always worthy of our sacrifice, the manly one, will strengthen our laud in preeminence.

Jamison Brereton Notes

sva├нtu- in b is a hapax. Following a tentative suggestion of GeldnerтАЩs (n. 9b), I take it as a vс╣Ыddhi form related to Aves. xv a─Уtu- тАШfamilyтАЩ, pace Narten (YH 266 n. 59), who, however, does not give reasons for her rejection of the association (though itтАЩs true that we should really expect a thematic *svaitava- or the like). I confess, however, that my rendering of ab is merely a guess (as, it seems, are the other divergent tr.). I donтАЩt know why the mountains should be associated with our production of offspring; the sexual connotation Witzel Got┼Н suggest in their n., that mountains are felsenhart and knotig, seems farfetched. My own tentative suggestion is that the progeny here belong to the mountains, not to us, and refer to the material goods originating from mountains that we will enjoy: see I.55.3 p├бrvataс╣Г n├б bh├│jase тАЬlike a mountain to be enjoyedтАЭ and GeldnerтАЩs parallels adduced there; also passages like VII.37.8 ─Б╠Бr─Б╠Бyo yantu p├бrvatasya r─Бta├║ тАЬlet the riches of the mountain come here at (the time for) givingтАЭ; II.24.2 v├бsumantam .. p├бrvatam тАЬthe goods-filled mountain.тАЭ If I am correct, the simile, in which the mountains are said to be v├бsavo n├б v─лr─Б╠Бс╕е тАЬlike good heroesтАЭ may be a bit of a pun, with v├бsavaс╕е actually referring to the material goods of the mountains. To make my interpr. clearer, I might slightly emend the tr. to тАЬto thrust out their progeny for us.тАЭ The alternative etym. of sva├нtu- found in Grassmann, favored by Narten, and represented in the tr. of Renou and Witzel Got┼Н analyses it as sv├б-etu- тАШhaving their own goingтАЩ, which seems singularly inappropriate. It is regularly emphasized that mountains canтАЩt be moved тАФ except when theyтАЩre in fear of some greater force (like the Maruts) тАФ so тАЬgoingтАЭ should not be one of their properities. It could refer to the myth of the winged mountains (the wings then clipped by Indra), but this does not seem the context for a reference to this myth. Witzel Got┼Н attenuate the sense to a figurative тАЬdie ein Eigenleben f├╝hren,тАЭ which avoids the mountain-movement problem, but essentially denies the force of the etymology. By contrast, a reference to тАШfamilyтАЩ fits comfortably with the production of progeny.

I donтАЩt know what ─Аptya is doing here, either. Again, the sexual connotation suggested in Witzel Got┼НтАЩs n. is invisible to me. It does seem likely that he is the same figure as Trita in 10b, since both are associated with the production of praise. Trita in 4b is less clearly tied in. Note ┼Ы├бс╣Гsaс╣Г n├бryaс╕е, which reminds of n├бr─Б-┼Ы├бс╣Гsa- (though they donтАЩt belong to the same syntagm here) and also continues the poetтАЩs fondness for -yaderivatives.

Griffith

Ours be the Parvatas, even they, for offspring, free-moving, who are Heroes like the Vasus.
May holy Aptya, Friend of man, exalted, strengthen our word for ever and be near us.

Geldner

Zur Fortpflanzung des Geschlechtes sollen uns die Berge g├╝nstig sein, die zu uns geh├╢ren wie die trefflichen M├дnner. Gelobt sei uns jederzeit der opferw├╝rdige Aptya; der Mannhafte best├дrke unter Bevorzugung unserer Rede.

F├╝r Kind und Enkel sei’n uns hold die Berge, und die wie edle M├дnner eignen Weg gehn, Der hehre Aptja, stets von uns gepriesen, der starke segne unsern Spruch mit Beistand.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI glorify with unqualified praise the embryo of the earth-fertilizing rain, the grandson of the waters, Agni, who is threefold, who rages (upon me) not, when travelling with (his) withering rays, but, bright-haired consumes the forests.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Earth-fertilizing rain: vс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зo bh┼лmyasya garbham: bh┼лmya = suited to the earth or the firmament, bh┼лmir antarkс╣гam; in the latter case, the embryo of the firmamental rain will mean Agni as the lightning; with his withering rays: gс╣Ыс╣З─лte agni etar─л na ┼Ы┼лс╣гaiс╕е = mayi gantari na krudhyati sukhakarai ra┼Ыmibhiс╕е, who is not angry upon me when going with his agreeable rays; but, ┼Ыuс╣гa = drying up

Jamison Brereton

I have praised the embryo of the terrestrial bull, (as) Trita (has praised) the Child of the Waters with a well-twisted (hymn).
Agni is sung with fortifying (hymns) like (a horse) at running.
Flame-haired, he liquefies the trees.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Witzel Got┼Н take Trita as the persona of the 1st ps. speaker of astoс╣гi (тАЬich, als Trita тАжтАЭ), whereas I follow Geldner and Renou in supplying a 3rd ps. form of тИЪstu for b.

The form et├бr─л is, of course, problematic, but is most likely a loc. sg.; for disc.

see Tichy (-tar-stems, 59-61). It is found only here and in VI.12.4, in the same p─Бdafinal phrase et├бr─л n├б ┼Ы┼лс╣гa├нс╕е. In our passage there is some phonetic justification for the form (though not in VI.12.4); note the ni/ri sylls: gr╠еn─лt├й agnir et├бr─л … / … n├н riс╣З─Бti.

Griffith

Trta praised him, germ of the earthly hero, with pure songs him the Offspring of the Waters.
Agn; with might neighs loudly like a charger: he of the flaming hair destroys the forests.

Geldner

Ich habe das Kind des irdischen Stieres gepriesen, als Trita mit sch├╢nem Loblied den Apam Napat. Agni wird gelobt wie ein Rennpferd mit anspornenden Worten, der Flammenhaarige macht die H├╢lzer klein.

Grassmann

Ich pries den Spross des erdgebornen Stieres, mit sch├╢nem Lied auch ihn, den Sohn der Wasser, Gepriesen wie die Wallerin mit Liedern verzehrt das Holz der flammenhaar’ge Agni.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHowcan we offer (fit praise) to the mighty posterity of Rudra, or to the all-knowing Bhaga, for (the sake of obtaining) riches; may the waters, may the plural nts, protect us, and the heaven, the woods, and the mountains, whose tresses are trees.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

How shall we speak to the great Rudrian (troop) [=Maruts]; what (shall we say) to observant Bhaga, for wealth?
Let the waters and the plants help us, and Heaven, the woods, and the mountains whose hair is trees.

Griffith

How shall we speak to the great might of Rudra? How speak to Bhaga who takes thought for riches?
May Plants, the Waters, and the Sky preserve us, and Woods and Mountains with their trees for tresses.

Geldner

Grassmann

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the lord of vigour, (V─Бyu), hear our prayers, he who traverses the firmament, the circumambient; may the waters hear, bright as cities, flowing round the towering mountains.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Bright as cities: puro na ┼Ыubhr─Бс╕е = pur─Бс╣Зi iva dipta, shining like cities

Jamison Brereton

Let him hear our hymnsтАФthe lord of nourishments; he [=Agni] is the vigorous encircler, passing more quickly than a cloud.
Let them hearтАФthe Waters, resplendent like the fortifications of a
mountain that encloses the offering ladles [=cows].

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. presents a number of difficulties. The first is the easiest solved: who is the referent of ab? Although this is almost universally taken to be the Wind, I think it is more likely Agni. Only Agni is called ┼лrj─Б╠Бm p├бti- тАЬlord of nourishmentsтАЭ (otherwise only in the voc. ┼лrj─Бm pate), also ┼лrj├│ n├бp─Бt тАЬchild of nourishment.тАЭ Given this exclusive identification, it seems unlikely that the audience would assign a different referent, esp. since ┼лrj─Б╠Бm p├бtiс╕е is the first epithet encountered and sets the frame of reference; the others only show up in p─Бda b. Moreover, though p├бrijman- тАШearth-circlingтАЩ is used of the Wind, it also refers to other entities, including, fairly often, Agni (VI.2.8, VI.13.2, VII.13.3, I.127.2, III.2.9). The other descriptor in b, iс╣гir├б- тАШvigorousтАЩ, is applied to a variety of beings and things, including the Wind, but also Agni (III.2.14, 5.4). The only activity posited of the subject of this hemistich is n├бbhas t├бr─лy─Бn (for which see below), which is also applicable to either.

The p─Бda-final s├б in p─Бda a is quite unusual. A cursory glance through Lubotsky for parallels yields only II.35.1, III.13.3, (VII.86.6 s─Б╠Б), IX.71.8, IX.79.3, X.108.4 (a careful search might produce a few more). All of these exx. are either rhetorically contrastive, or s├б takes its proper position in a new clause. Although it is possible that the s├б here also begins a new, purely nominal clause with b, this seems clumsy. I have a quite speculative suggestion about it, linking it with the immediately following n├бbhas t├бr─лy─Бn. The standard тАФ and quite persuasive тАФ interpr. of this phrase is тАЬquicker than a cloud,тАЭ but this imposes an abl. sg. interpr. on n├бbhaс╕е, which should then belong to a root noun n├бbh- тАШcloudтАЩ, beside the standard s-stem n├бbhas-. This root noun does not otherwise exist: the supposed root noun n├бbh- (glossed тАШZerspalter, ZerbrecherтАЩ by Grassmann) in I.174.8 is more likely a verb (see comm. ad loc.). And in any case we should expect an accent *nabh├бs. RenouтАЩs suggestion that n├бbhas is simply haplology for *n├бbhasas is probably correct, but I suggest that it left a trace of its vanished final -as in the p─Бda-final s├б immediately preceding тАФ a tangible sign of the effects of speed: the final syllable got cut off and left behind.

The second hemistich is very puzzling and has given rise to very different and incompatible interpr. (Witzel Got┼Н being esp. distant from the rest). Mine more or less follows Oldenberg (or one of his alternatives), who discusses the passage with his customary acuity; I will not discuss other renderings in detail. I am not at all certain that mine (/OldenbergтАЩs) is correct, however. The framework of the passage compares the waters, subjects of the verb, with fortifications (p├║raс╕е), the point of comparison being their resplendant appearance (┼Ыubhr├б-). So far also Geldner; Renou also follows this structure, but floats the possibility that p├║r- can mean тАШcorpsтАЩ, which would be convenient but is of course unsupported. With Oldenberg and Geldner (we now lose Renou, who takes d as a separate clause with the ladles as subj.), the fortifications are those of a mountain (├бdreс╕е), and this mountain is characterized as p├бri тАж babс╣Ыh─Бс╣З├б- тАШenclosingтАЩ (p├бri тИЪbс╣Ыh has this meaning in the Br─Бh.). Although we would not ordinarily expect tmesis of a participle, esp. a part. in an oblique case, the tmesis here is iconic: the enclosed object is located between preverb and participle. This object is sr├║caс╕е тАШoffering ladlesтАЩ. Now of course in a literal interpr. a mountain enclosing a bunch of ladles sounds very odd, Oldenberg cleverly suggests that the ladles stand for cows – living ladles, as it were, from which ghee comes as it does from the offering ladles. These cows are then the cows trapped within the Vala cave. The hemistich thus starts jointly in the physical world and on the ritual grounds, since the listening waters are probably both тАЬrealтАЭ natural waters and the waters standing by for the soma sacrifice.

It then moves, via the simile, to the natural world (mountain fortifications) and the world of myth (the Vala cave), and back to the ritual ground, with the enclosed ladles.

If this interpr. is correct, it is a very condensed and clever expression.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMighty Maruts, of goodly aspect, quickly hear (the praises) that we who repair to you repeat, offering acceptable (oblations); (the Maruts) coming hither, well disposed, come down to us, (destroying) with their weapons the mortals opposed to them, (overcome) by agitation.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Just by our knowledge, o great ones [=Maruts], we shall say which are your ways, wondrous ones, as we acquire what is choice.
And like birds, those of good essence [=Maruts] swoop down here
in pursuit with their fluttering to the mortal held by murderous
weapons.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Another opaque vs., whose difficulties begin with the first word vid─Б╠Б. This is taken as the 2nd pl. pf. by Grassmann, Geldner, Witzel Got┼Н. (Renou unaccountably takes it as a 1st sg. тАШJe sais тАжтАЩ, without comment – presumably a careless error for v├йda.) I follow Oldenberg in taking it as the instr. of the root noun to the same root.

The phrase y├й va ├йv─Б(с╕е) recurs from 5d though in a different metrical position.

Here as there it refers to the тАЬwaysтАЭ (├йv─Бс╕е) of the Maruts (so Geldner, Renou, flg. S─Бyaс╣Зa., contra OldenbergтАЩs tentative ─Аdityas) – the ways which by our knowledge (vid─Б╠Б) we are in a position to proclaim (br├бv─Бma), presumably in the form of a hymn, for which we expect reward (v─Б╠Бryaс╣Г d├бdh─Бn─Бс╕е тАЬacquiring what is choiceтАЭ) – just as in vs. 5 a visionary thought (dh─л╠Бс╕е) was to be produced in return for wealth (r─Бy├б ├йс╣гe ├бvase тАЬfor help in the quest for wealthтАЭ). The part. d├бdh─Бn─Бс╕е has almost a purpose function, and to make the reciprocal action clearer I might emend the tr. from тАЬas we acquireтАЭ to тАЬwhile acquiring тАжтАЭ or even тАЬfor acquiring.тАЭ The first sticking point in the second hemistich is can├б. This is universally taken as negative (as can├б generally is). However, in this case I think that it is simply equivalent to ca n├б (so also Klein I: 289-91 with n. 8) and that the n├б here is serving as the simile-marking particle, not the negative. v├бyaс╕е is often used in a simile at the beginning of a p─Бda: I count 7 #v├бyo n├б passages, incl. V.59.7 in this maс╣Зс╕Нala, where itтАЩs the Maruts who are compared to birds (cf. also I.87.2 #v├бya iva marutaс╕е) тАФ though I do have to admit that 2 #v├бya┼Ы can├б passages (I.24.6, 155.5) contain the negative.

Therefore, contra all the standard tr./interpr., I take the subject of cd not as тАШbirdsтАЩ (v├бyaс╕е), but as the Maruts compared to birds (like V.59.7, I.87.2). The adj.

subh┼л╠Б- тАШof good essenceтАЩ is regularly used of the Maruts in this maс╣Зс╕Нala (V.55.3, 59.3, 87.3) and would identify them as the referent to an alert audience. In this 2nd half-vs. we make good on our promise to proclaim the ways of the Maruts – this exploit is one of these ways.

Unfortunately exactly what that exploit involves is unclear. That the Maruts should come down like birds is unproblematic: they regularly fly through the midspace and come down to interact with mortals, generally at the ritual. But the target of their descent, expressed in p─Бda d, has no parallels, as far as I can find. In my interpr. the mortal (m├бrtam) to whom they come is in distress and receives their help. Unlike the standard tr. I take the hapax root noun instr. kс╣гubh─Б╠Бas characterizing the MarutsтАЩ movements (fluttering like birds), not the state of the mortal, which is expressed by ├бnuyataс╣Г vadhasna├нс╕е тАЬheld/controlled by murderous weapons.тАЭ I assume that he is under attack by hostile forces and requires the MarutsтАЩ assistance to free him.

The phonological play with va/─Б that we noted earlier in the hymn (particularly vss. 1, 5) has returned here: тАж y├й va ev─Б╠Б, br├бv─Бma …v─Б╠Бryaс╣Г …

v├бya(с╕е) … subhv├а(с╕е) … vadhasna├нс╕е тАФ which draws attention to the thematic connection between this vs. and vs. 5.

рджреИрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдирд┐ рджреЗрд╡рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзреАрдирд┐ рдкрд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рд╡рд╛рдирд┐ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реАрд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзреАрдирд┐ рдЪ рдЬрдиреНрдо рдЬрдиреНрдорд╛рдирд┐ рдЕрдкрд╢реНрдЪ рдЕрдкрд╕рд╛ рдЕрдЪреНрдЫ рдЕрднрд┐рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддреБрдВ рд╕реБрдордЦрд╛рдп рд╢реЛрднрдирдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдп рдорд░реБрджреНрдЧрдгрд╛рдп рд╡реЛрдЪрдВ рдмреНрд░рд╡реАрдорд┐ ред рдЧрд┐рд░рдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддрдпрдГ рд╡рд░реНрдзрдиреНрддрд╛рдореН ред рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рдГ рджреНрдпреЛрддрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рд╕реНрд╡рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкрд╛рджреНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдердкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рд┐рдиреНрдпрдГ рдЪрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рдЧреНрд░рд╛рдГ ред рдЖрд╣реНрд▓рд╛рджрдирдВ рд╣рд┐рд░рдгреНрдпрдВ рд╡рд╛рдЧреНрд░реЗ рдпрд╛рд╕рд╛рдВ рддрд╛рдГ ред рддрд╛рджреГрд╢реНрдпрдГ рд╕рддреНрдпреЛ рд╡рд░реНрдзрдиреНрддрд╛рдореН ред рдЕрд░реНрдгрд╛рдГ рдирджреНрдпрд╢реНрдЪ рдЕрднрд┐рд╖рд╛рддрд╛рдГ рдорд░реБрджреНрднрд┐рдГ рд╕рдВрднрдХреНрддрд╛рдГ рдЙрджрд╛ рдЙрджрдХреЗрди рд╡рд░реНрдзрдиреНрддрд╛рдВ рд╕рдореГрджреНрдзрд╛ рднрд╡рдиреНрддреБ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI offer adoration to the company of the Maruts deserving of sacred sacrifice, to obtain the waters, whether born of heaven or earth; may my praises prosper; may the joy-bestowing heavens (flourish); may the rivers cherished (by the Maruts) be filled with water.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

I will call on the heavenly and earthly breeds and on the waters for the good battler (/very bounteous one) [=Indra].
Let the days increase and the hymns tipped with gold; let the waters, the conquered floods increase.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Since Indra is several times called s├║makha-, I assume he is the referent here – though nothing much depends on it in this generic vs. and both Geldner and Renou take it to be the sacrificer or the patron of the sacrifice.

Witzel Got┼Н suggest that candr─Б╠Бgr─Б(с╕е) modifies both тАШdaysтАЩ and тАШhymnsтАЩ; this is a good idea, with тАШgold, gleamтАЩ used in two slightly different senses. The days begin with the gleaming of the golden sun, while the hymns offered to the gods are metaphorically tipped with the gold given by the gods in response to praise.

In d ud─Б╠Бis generally taken as the instr. sg. of a root noun тАШwaterтАЩ (so, e.g., Grassmann and all the standard tr., though Geldner hesitates), beside the more common oblique nstem instr. udn─Б╠Б. However, I follow Schindler (Root nouns, 12-13), who argues that it is better taken as the nom./acc. pl. to the same -n-stem.

The somewhat curious expression abh├нс╣г─Бt─Б ├бrс╣З─Бс╕е тАЬconquered floodsтАЭ finds its formulaic match in nearby V.50.4 ├бrс╣З─Б тАж s├бnit─Б тАШwinner of the floodsтАЩ; this may well be a general reference to the progress of the ─Аrya into the Punjab, winning territory river by river. Geldner cites as parallel I.131.5 t├й any─Б╠Бm-any─Бс╣Г nady├аm saniс╣гnata тАЬThey kept winning one river after another.тАЭ

Griffith

Celestial and terrestrial generations, and Waters will I summon to the feasting.
May days with bright dawns cause my songs to prosper, and may the conquered streams increase their waters.

Geldner

Die g├╢ttlichen und die irdischen Geschlechter und die Gew├дsser rufe ich her f├╝r den Freigebigen. Es sollen sich die Tage, die Reden, die Gold im Munde haben, mehren; an Wasser sollen die errungenen Fl├╝sse zunehmen.

Grassmann

Ich ruf’ des Himmels und der Erde St├дmme, die Wasser ruf’ ich her dem tapfern Helden; Es seien stark die hohen, lichten Himmel, die Fluten stark an Wogen, die errungnen.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрдзрд┐рдордиреНрддреНрд░рдореН (VC)
  • рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реЗрджреЗрд╡рд╛:

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдлрд┐рд░ рдЙрд╕реА рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХреЛ рдХрд╣рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛ ! рдореИрдВ рдЬрд┐рди (рджреИрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдирд┐) рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрда рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рд╣реБрдП (рдкрд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рд╡рд╛рдирд┐) рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реАрдВ рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд┐рджрд┐рдд (рдЬрдиреНрдо) рдЬрдиреНрдореЛрдВ рдФрд░ (рдЕрдкрдГ) рдХрд░реНрдореНрдореЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рдЪ) рднреА (рдЕрдЪреНрдЫрд╛) рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ (рдЖ, рд╡реЛрдЪрдореН) рд╕рдм рдУрд░ рд╕реЗ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢ рдХрд░реВрдБ рдЬрд┐рд╕ (рдЙрджрд╛) рдЬрд▓ рд╕реЗ (рдЕрд░реНрдгрд╛рдГ) рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░реЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╕рджреГрд╢ рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреА (рдЪрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рдЧреНрд░рд╛рдГ) рд╕реБрд╡рд░реНрдг рд╡рд╛ рдЖрдирдиреНрдж рдЕрдЧреНрд░реЗ рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рдкрд░рд┐рдгрд╛рдо рджрд╢рд╛ рдореЗрдВ рдЬрд┐рдирдХреЗ рдЙрди (рдЕрднрд┐рд╖рд╛рддрд╛рдГ) рдЪрд╛рд░реЛрдВ рдУрд░ рд╕реЗ рдмрдБрдЯреА рд╣реБрдИ (рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рдГ) рд╕рддреНрдп рдХрд╛рдордирд╛рдУрдВ рдХреЛ рдФрд░ (рдЧрд┐рд░рдГ) рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдд рд╡рд╛рдгрд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХреА (рд╡рд░реНрдзрдиреНрддрд╛рдореН) рд╡реГрджреНрдзрд┐ рдХреАрдЬрд┐рдпреЗ рдЬрд┐рд╕рд╕реЗ (рд╕реБрдордЦрд╛рдп) рд╢реЛрднрди рдпрдЬреНрдЮреЛрдВрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХреА (рд╡рд░реНрдзрдиреНрддрд╛рдореН) рд╡реГрджреНрдзрд┐ рд╣реЛ реерезрекрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИ ред рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛ ! рдЖрдк рд▓реЛрдЧ рдзрд░реНрдореНрдордпреБрдХреНрдд рдХрд░реНрдореНрдореЛрдВ рдФрд░ рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрда рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдг рдХрд░рдХреЗ рдЕрдкрдиреА рдХрд╛рдордирд╛рдУрдВ рдФрд░ рд╡рд╛рдгреА рдХреЛ рд╢реЛрднрд┐рдд рдХрд░реЛ, рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рдЬрд▓ рд╕реЗ рдирджрд┐рдпрд╛рдБ рдФрд░ рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░ рдмреЭрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рд╣реА рдзрд░реНрдореНрдордпреБрдХреНрдд рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрде рд╕реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рдмреЭрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ реерезрекрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ ! рдЕрд╣рдВ рдпрд╛рдирд┐ рджреИрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдирд┐ рдкрд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рд╡рд╛рдирд┐ рдЬрдиреНрдорд╛рдкрд╢реНрдЪрд╛рдЪреНрдЫрд╛рд╜рд╜рд╡реЛрдЪрдВ рдпреЗрдиреЛрджрд╛ рдЕрд░реНрдгрд╛ рдЗрд╡рд╛рд╜рд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рдЪрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рдЧреНрд░рд╛ рдЕрднрд┐рд╖рд╛рддрд╛ рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡реЛ рдЧрд┐рд░рд╢реНрдЪ рд╡рд░реНрдзрдиреНрддрд╛рдореН рдпрддрдГ рд╕реБрдордЦрд╛рдп рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐рдиреЛ рд╡рд░реНрдзрдиреНрддрд╛рдореН реерезрекрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЖ) рд╕рдордиреНрддрд╛рддреН (рджреИрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдирд┐) рджреЗрд╡реЗрд╖реБ рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпреЗрд╖реБ рдЧреБрдгреЗрд╖реБ рднрд╡рд╛рдирд┐ (рдкрд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рд╡рд╛рдирд┐) рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рджрд┐рддрд╛рдирд┐ (рдЬрдиреНрдо) рдЬрдиреНрдорд╛рдирд┐ (рдЕрдкрдГ) рдЕрдкрд╛рдВрд╕рд┐ рдХрд░реНрдореНрдорд╛рдгрд┐ (рдЪ) (рдЕрдЪреНрдЫрд╛) рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╕рдВрд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдпрд╛рдорд┐рддрд┐ рджреАрд░реНрдШрдГред (рд╕реБрдордЦрд╛рдп) рд╢реЛрднрдирд╛ рдордЦрд╛ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛ рдпрд╕реНрдп рддрд╕реНрдореИ (рд╡реЛрдЪрдореН) рдЙрдкрджрд┐рд╢реЗрдпрдореН (рд╡рд░реНрдзрдиреНрддрд╛рдореН) (рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рдГ) рд╕рддреНрдпрд╛рдГ рдХрд╛рдорд╛рдГ (рдЧрд┐рд░рдГ) рд╕реБрд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд┐рддрд╛ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдГ (рдЪрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рдЧреНрд░рд╛рдГ) рдЪрдиреНрджреНрд░рдВ рд╕реБрд╡рд░реНрдгрдорд╛рдирдиреНрджреЛ рд╡рд╛рд╜рдЧреНрд░реЗ рдпрд╛рд╕рд╛рдВ рддрд╛рдГ (рдЙрджрд╛) рдЙрджрдХреЗрди (рд╡рд░реНрдзрдиреНрддрд╛рдореН) (рдЕрднрд┐рд╖рд╛рддрд╛рдГ) рдЕрднрд┐рддреЛ рд╡рд┐рднрдХреНрддрд╛рдГ (рдЕрд░реНрдгрд╛рдГ) рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░рд╛рдГ реерезрекрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMy praise has been continually proffered as a protectress, powerful with (the means of) preservation; may the maternal and venerable earth accept our (praises), and, (plural ased) with her pious (worshippers) be (to us) straight-handed, and the giver of good.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

As a protectress: var┼лtr─л = asmad upadravavarayitr─л, what or who keeps off oppression upon us

Jamison Brereton

Step after step old age has been secured for me, either (by her) who is the able Shielding Goddess or by the protectors.
Let the mother, the great Ras─Б, accompany us along with our patrons, she with hands outstretched, with winnings outstretched.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The action in p─Бda a is a positive one: the speaker is assured to make it to old age. See 17de and disc. there, as well as X.59.4, which will be disc. further below.

The construction in b, which expresses the agent of n├н dh─Бyi, is complex. Its underlying model is the тАЬX and which YтАЭ construction, but it is inverted, with the rel.

cl. member first: тАЬ(by her) who is тАж and by the protectors.тАЭ Moreover, it contains both v─Б and ca. As Klein says (II.174-75), тАЬthe construction should most likely be viewed as a conjunctive anacoluthon in which the poet begins by intending alternative conjunction and finishes with an additive sequence. Within each member the conjunction occupies its normal enclitic position: (v├бr┼лtr─л v─Б ┼Ыakr─Б y─Б╠Б) (p─Бy├║bhi┼Ы ca).тАЭ On с╣Ыjuv├бniс╕е see Scarlatta 467-68. Note that this form produces a bad cadence.

On the connection between cd and vss. 19-20 see disc. below.

Griffith

Duly to each one hath my laud been offered. Strong be Varutri with her powers to succour.
May the great Mother Rasa here befriend us, straight-handed, with the princes, striving forward.

Geldner

Auf Schritt und Tritt sei mir das Alter sichergestellt, sei es durch die m├дchtige Varutri und durch die Schutzgeister. Es sollen uns samt den Lohnherren die gro├Яe Mutter Rasa zur Seite stehen, die eine redliche Hand hat, die redlichen Gewinn bringt.

Grassmann

Bewahrt sei Schritt f├╝r Schritt mein Lebensalter; die Schirmerin sei stark mit ihren H├╝tern; Es sei uns hold die Flut, die grosse Mutter, die mit den F├╝rsten Hand ausstreckend vordringt.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHow may we (duly) worship the liberal (Maruts) with praise, how adore the Maruts with present praise in a fitting manner, the glorious Maruts with present praise? may Ahirbudhnya contrive nor for our harm; may he be the destroyer (of our enemies).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

How might we ritually serve with reverence those of good drops, the Maruts traveling their ways, at the invitationтАФthe Maruts of
advancing fame, at the invitation?
Let Ahi Budhnya not set us up to suffer harm. For us let there be
winnings at the distribution (of prizes).

Jamison Brereton Notes

As does upam─Бtiv├бniс╕е in 16e. On this form and on the meter of both -v├бniс╕е forms, see Scarlatta 467. On ├║pam─Бti- see comm. ad VIII.40.9.

The opening of the vs., kath─Б╠Бd─Б┼Ыema, echoes 11a kath─Б╠БтАж brav─Бma. In both cases the object of our action is the Maruts. Another echo is found in evay─Б╠Б(с╕е), which is a scrambling of y├й va ├йv─Б(с╕е) of 5d and 13a (though y├й and -y─Б(с╕е) are completely different grammatically), in both cases of the Maruts. The sequence in our p─Бda b, evay─Б╠Бmar├║taс╕е тАЬthe Maruts traveling their ways,тАЭ is also matched by the punctuating exclamation evay─Б╠Бmarut found in every vs. of the Anhangslied to the Maruts that ends this maс╣Зс╕Нala (V.87.1-9, tr. there тАЬMaruts on the marchтАЭ).

Griffith

How may we serve the Liberal Ones with worship, the Maruts swift of course in invocation, the Maruts far-renowned in invocation?
Let not the Dragon of the Deep annoy us, and gladly may he welcome our addresses.

Geldner

Wie sollen wir unter Verbeugung den gabensch├╢nen Marut aufwarten, die aus eigenem Antrieb auf die Einladung hin kommen, die weitber├╝hmten Marut auf die Einladung hin? Nicht soll uns Ahi Budhnya zu Schaden bringen; f├╝r uns sei er der Gewinner von Schenkungen.

Grassmann

Wie dienen wir den gabenreichen Maruts, den eilend gehnden andachtsvoll beim Anruf? Der Wetterdrache geb uns nicht dem Feind hin, er sei’s, der freundlich unsre Rede annimmt.

Elizarenkova

рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

рд╣реЗ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рд╕рдГ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ рд╡рдГ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдиреН рдЗрддрд┐ рдЪрд┐рддреН рдЗрддреНрдердореЗрд╡ рдиреБ рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рдВ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдпреИ рдкрд╢реБрдорддреНрдпреИ рдкрд╢реБрд╕рд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдпрд╛рдкрддреНрдпрд╛рдп рд╡рдирддреЗ рднрдЬрддреЗ рдорд░реНрддреНрдпрдГ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирдГ ред рдЖ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рд╕рдГ рдЗрддрд┐ рдкреБрдирд░реБрдХреНрддрд┐рд░рд╛рджрд░рд╛рд░реНрдерд╛ред рдЕрддреНрд░ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рдпрдЬреНрдЮреЗ рд╢рд┐рд╡рд╛рдВ рдзрд╛рд╕рд┐рдореН рдЕрдиреНрдирдВ рдореЗ рдордо рдЕрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдГ рддрдиреНрд╡рдГ рджреЗрд╡реИрд░рдиреБрдЧреГрд╣реАрддрд╕реНрдп рдкреБрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рдХрд░реЛрддреБ рдирд┐рд░реНрдЛрддрд┐рдГ рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛ ред рдЬрд░рд╛рдВ рдЪрд┐рддреН рдЬрд░рд╛рдВ рдЪ рдЬрдЧреНрд░рд╕реАрдд рдЧреНрд░рд╕рддреБ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe mortal (sacrificer) worships you, gods, at all times for progeny and cattle; verily, gods, the mortal worships you; may Nirс╣Ыti, on this occasion, sustain my body with salutary food, and keep off decay.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

In just these words now, for the sake of offspring along with cattle, the mortal (seeks to) win you, o godsтАФthe mortal (seeks to) win you
here, o gods.
Otherwise Dissolution might swallow the secure depository beneficial to this body, my own old age.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, vss. 16-17, in a different meter from what precedes (and follows), seem to provide a summary of the preceding hymn, esp. 17, with its self-conscious internal quote ├нti cin n├║ тАЬin just these (words) now.тАЭ See Janert (Dh─Бsi, pp. 16-17), who argues this position in some detail.

All the standard tr. (as well as Janert, 42) agree in taking d and e as separate clauses and supplying a verb for c. All consider the clauses contrastive: in d I hope to be granted a pleasant or benevolent dh─Бs├н- for my body, while in e I express the wish that Nirс╣Ыti should swallow my old age. But this is directly contrary to what was said in 15ab, where the securing of his old age was an occasion for celebration by the poet.

It is true that two different words for тАШold ageтАЩ are involved: jarim├бn- in 15, jar─Б╠Б- in 17, but these words do not contrast semantically elsewhere as far as I can see (cf. X.32.5, 8, which contains jar─Б╠Б- followed by jarim├бn-) (even though Renou remarks тАЬnoter lтАЩoppositionтАЭ). An important parallel is provided by X.59.4 dy├║bhir hit├│ jarim─Б╠Бs┼л╠Бno astu, par─Бtar├бс╣Г s├║ n├нrс╣Ыtir jih─лt─Бm тАЬThroughout the days let our old age be secured for us. – Let Dissolution move herself further away.тАЭ There old age is тАШsecuredтАЩ (hit├бс╕е) as it was in our 15a jarim─Б╠Бn├н dh─Бyi (both to тИЪdh─Б), and Dissolution (n├нrс╣Ыtiс╕е) is urged to move away. (It should be admitted that that p─Бda is a refrain to the first three vss. of X.59 and so not necessarily as closely tied to the preceding p─Бda as it might be.) I therefore doubt that in our vs. the poet is hoping that Dissolution will swallow the old age that he (and other poets) elsewhere want to keep safe.

Instead I think de is the expression of his fear that if he fails to win the gods (abc) Dissolution will succeed in depriving him of his wished-for old age. I have pushed ├бtr─Б perhaps a bit too much – to тАШotherwiseтАЩ; I would prefer a тАШlestтАЩ (n├йd) clause or even a m─Б╠Бclause, but n├йd, which becomes well developed in Vedic prose, barely exists in the RV and the poet may have been casting about for a way to express this modality. A further piece of evidence in favor of my interpr. is the word dh─Бs├н.

Although this word often means тАШwell-springтАЩ or тАШsourceтАЩ (see comm. ad I.62.3, 140.1), in some cases it seems to mean тАШplace, depositoryтАЩ and be associated with (/derived, at least synchronically, from) тИЪdh─Б. Here the dh─Бs├н- seems to be the nominalization of n├н dh─Бyi in 15 (cf. hit├бс╕е in X.58.4) тАФ that is, the place in which old age is securely held. I therefore take it as coreferential with jar─Б╠Бm in e. _________ 18-20 If, as suggested above, 16-17 are the finale of the hymn proper, these 3 (or 2 ┬╝) were tacked on. They certainly lack the complications of the rest of the hymn. The dominance of female figures is striking.

Griffith

Thus thinking, O ye Gods, the mortal wins you to give him increase of his herds of cattle: the mortal wins him, O ye Gods, your favour.
Here he wins wholesome food to feed this body: as for mine old age, Nirrti consume it

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDivine Vasus, may we obtain from the adorable cow invigorating and mind-sustaining food; may that liberal and benignant goddess, hastening (I, her), come for our felicity.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Might we obtain that favor of yours, o gods, good ones, the nourishing refreshment of the cow, through (this) recitation.
That gracious goddess of good drops [/gifts] should come toward us at a run, for our welfare.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Despite the word order, I follow Janert (contra the standard tr.) in construing p─Бda-final g├│с╕е with ├нс╣гam, rather than with immediately preceding ┼Ы├бs─Б, which saves us from determining what the recitation or instruction of the cow is.

Griffith

O Gods, may we obtain from you this favour, strengthening food through the Cow’s praise, ye Vasus.
May she who gives good gifts, the gracious Goddes. s, come speeding nigh to us for our well-being.

Geldner

Diese Gunst von euch, ihr G├╢tter, das st├дrkende Labsal m├╢chten wir erlangen, ihr Guten, durch die Zusage einer Kuh. Diese gabensch├╢ne, barmherzige G├╢ttin m├╢ge eilig uns entgegenkommen zur Wohlfahrt.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay Iс╕╖─Б, the mother of the herd, and Urva┼Ы─л with the rivers, be favourable to us; may the bright-shining Urva┼Ы─л (come), commanding our devotion, and investing the worshipper with light.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Iс╕╖─Б and Urva┼Ы─л: iс╕╖─Б = the earth, or the daughter of Manu, in the form of a cow, the mother of the herd, y┼лthasya m─Бt─Б; or, the latter may be applied to the company of the Maruts, when Iс╕╖─Б may be madhyamik─Б v─Бk, middle, articulate or human speech; or, the latter sense may be applied to Urva┼Ы─л; investing the worshipper with light: abhy┼лrс╣Зarv─Бn─Б prabhс╣Ыthasy─Б yoс╕е: the latter term should be read ayum, in the accusative ative, man or the yajam─Бna;

Prabhс╣Ыta = light, tejas, or water, udakam (Nirukta 2.49) and being in the genitive tive, requires d─Бnena, by the gift of; or, the ellipse may be filled up by yaj├▒am, when the sentence will be: covering or protecting the sacrifice of the man making the offering

Jamison Brereton Notes

The single p─Бda of 20 simply continues vs. 19 thematically and syntactically, as Oldenberg points out. They constitute a single vs. The signature word of the beginning of the hymn, v─Б, returns in force: urv├б┼Ы─л v─Б …urv├б┼Ы─л v─Б brhaddi ╠е v─Б╠Б… ┼лrс╣Зv─Бn─Б╠Б. Note also urv├б┼Ы─л … urv├б┼Ы─л … abhy┼лrс╣Зv─Бn─Б╠Б…

┼лrjavy├аsya.

This vs. sequence seems inspired by 15cd. Vs. 15 has a similar focus on female figures, and 15c #s├нс╣гaktu m─Бt─Б╠Бmah─л╠Бras─Б╠Бnaс╕е is echoed by 20a #s├нс╣гaktu naс╕е, whose subject is likewise a female. The тАШmotherтАЩ m─Бt─Б╠Бof 15c is matched slightly earlier in this vs. sequence, in 19a, and there she is accompanied by rivers (sm├бn nad─л╠Бbhiс╕е 19b), even as the mother of 15c is identified as the river Ras─Б.

In fact 19-20 depict a matriarchal lineage of sorts, as Geldner points out (n. 19bc).

Besides Iс╕Н─Б, explicitly тАЬthe mother of the flockтАЭ (y┼лth├бsya m─Бt─Б╠Б) here, there is Urva┼Ы─л, twice: 19b and 19c. I am not entirely sure what to make of this doubling. I doubt that two different Urva┼Ы─лs are meant, rather the familiar Urva┼Ы─л in two different guises (so Geldner). In 19b she is associated with rivers. This reminds us of the attendance of her fellow Apsarases and of the rivers on the birth of Urva┼Ы─лтАЩs son in X.95.6-7, with Urva┼Ы─л herself qualified as тАШwateryтАЩ (├бpy─Б in X.95.10b) and her son as тАЬborn from the waterтАЭ (j├бniс╣гс╣нo ap├бс╕е, X.95.10c). Urva┼Ы─л Bс╣Ыhaddiv─Б (тАШof lofty heavenтАЩ; on the accent bс╣Ыhaddiv─Б╠Б- see AiG II.1.109, 120) in 19c may refer to a return to her residence in heaven after breaking with Pur┼лravas (not, however, mentioned in X.95). In any case, Urva┼Ы─лтАЩs son is named ─Аyu; his paternal grandmother is Iс╕Н─Б, the mother of Pur┼лravas (addresed as aiс╕Нa in X.95.18), so the title тАШmotherтАЩ given to Iс╕Н─Б in 19a has another resonance. Because of Urva┼Ы─лтАЩs relationship to ─Аyu, with Geldner and Renou I supply тАШmotherтАЩ in 19d and 20a to govern the various genitives. Thus with Iс╕Н─Б, Urva┼Ы─л, and ─Аyu we have a three-generational family.

I am uncertain what to do with ┼лravy├аsya in 20 (PN or not), and I also do not know what abhy┼лrс╣Зv─Бс╣З─Б╠Бin 19d is conveying.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The single p─Бda of 20 simply continues vs. 19 thematically and syntactically, as Oldenberg points out. They constitute a single vs. The signature word of the beginning of the hymn, v─Б, returns in force: urv├б┼Ы─л v─Б …urv├б┼Ы─л v─Б brhaddi ╠е v─Б╠Б… ┼лrс╣Зv─Бn─Б╠Б. Note also urv├б┼Ы─л … urv├б┼Ы─л … abhy┼лrс╣Зv─Бn─Б╠Б…

┼лrjavy├аsya.

This vs. sequence seems inspired by 15cd. Vs. 15 has a similar focus on female figures, and 15c #s├нс╣гaktu m─Бt─Б╠Бmah─л╠Бras─Б╠Бnaс╕е is echoed by 20a #s├нс╣гaktu naс╕е, whose subject is likewise a female. The тАШmotherтАЩ m─Бt─Б╠Бof 15c is matched slightly earlier in this vs. sequence, in 19a, and there she is accompanied by rivers (sm├бn nad─л╠Бbhiс╕е 19b), even as the mother of 15c is identified as the river Ras─Б.

In fact 19-20 depict a matriarchal lineage of sorts, as Geldner points out (n. 19bc).

Besides Iс╕Н─Б, explicitly тАЬthe mother of the flockтАЭ (y┼лth├бsya m─Бt─Б╠Б) here, there is Urva┼Ы─л, twice: 19b and 19c. I am not entirely sure what to make of this doubling. I doubt that two different Urva┼Ы─лs are meant, rather the familiar Urva┼Ы─л in two different guises (so Geldner). In 19b she is associated with rivers. This reminds us of the attendance of her fellow Apsarases and of the rivers on the birth of Urva┼Ы─лтАЩs son in X.95.6-7, with Urva┼Ы─л herself qualified as тАШwateryтАЩ (├бpy─Б in X.95.10b) and her son as тАЬborn from the waterтАЭ (j├бniс╣гс╣нo ap├бс╕е, X.95.10c). Urva┼Ы─л Bс╣Ыhaddiv─Б (тАШof lofty heavenтАЩ; on the accent bс╣Ыhaddiv─Б╠Б- see AiG II.1.109, 120) in 19c may refer to a return to her residence in heaven after breaking with Pur┼лravas (not, however, mentioned in X.95). In any case, Urva┼Ы─лтАЩs son is named ─Аyu; his paternal grandmother is Iс╕Н─Б, the mother of Pur┼лravas (addresed as aiс╕Нa in X.95.18), so the title тАШmotherтАЩ given to Iс╕Н─Б in 19a has another resonance. Because of Urva┼Ы─лтАЩs relationship to ─Аyu, with Geldner and Renou I supply тАШmotherтАЩ in 19d and 20a to govern the various genitives. Thus with Iс╕Н─Б, Urva┼Ы─л, and ─Аyu we have a three-generational family.

I am uncertain what to do with ┼лravy├аsya in 20 (PN or not), and I also do not know what abhy┼лrс╣Зv─Бс╣З─Б╠Бin 19d is conveying.

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ рдЬрдЧрддреН рдХрд╛ рдЙрдкрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рд╡рд╣реА рд╕рдореНрдкреВрд░реНрдг рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдУрдВ рдХреЗ рд╕рдореНрдмрдиреНрдз рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╣реИ реереирежрее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реЗрджреЗрд╡реЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдг рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рдХрд░рдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдЗрд╕ рд╕реЗ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее рдпрд╣ рдЗрдХрддрд╛рд▓реАрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рд╕реЛрд▓рд╣рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рдпреЛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рднрд╡реЗрддреН рд╕ рди рдКрд░реНрдЬрд╡реНрдпрд╕реНрдп рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯреЗрд░реНрдпреЛрдЧрдВ рд╕рд┐рд╖рдХреНрддреБ реереирежрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╕рд┐рд╖рдХреНрддреБ) рдкрд░рд┐рдЪрд░рддреБ (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН (рдКрд░реНрдЬрд╡реНрдпрд╕реНрдп) рдмрд╣реБрдмрд▓рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд╕реНрдп (рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯреЗрдГ) реереирежрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпреЛ рдЬрдЧрджреБрдкрдХрд╛рд░реА рднрд╡рддрд┐ рд╕ рдПрд╡ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╕рдореНрдмрдиреНрдзрдВ рдХрд░реНрддреНрддреБрдорд░реНрд╣рддрд┐ реереирежрее рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрди рдХреГрддрдорддреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдп рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддреНрдпреЗрдХрдЪрддреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╖реЛрдбрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ рдЬрдЧрд╛рд╡рд░ рдЙрдкрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рдгрд╛рд░рд╛ рдЕрд╕рддреЛ рддреЛрдЪ рд╕рдВрдкреВрд░реНрдг рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреЗрд╢реА рд╕рдВрд▓рдЧреНрди рдЕрд╕рддреЛ. рее реиреж рее
